  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d2425b32-78c4-4f99-99c8-c748f56634ee'
      });

  <span id="freeText5320573988777786972" style="display:none">This one's double the fun!<br /><br />Bounty hunter Stephanie Plum is still learning the ropes at her cousin Vinnie's bail bond office, so when she sets out on the trail of Kenny Mancuso - a suspiciously wealthy, working class Trenton boy who has just shot his best friend - the stakes are higher than ever. That Mancuso is distantly related to vice cop Joe Morelli - who is trying to beat Stephanie to the punch - only makes the hunt more thrilling...<br /><br />Taking pointers from her bounty hunter pal, Ranger, and using her pistol packing Grandma Mazur as a decoy, Stephanie is soon closing in on her mark. But Morelli and his libido are worthy foes. And a more sinister kind of enemy has made his first move... and his next move might be Stephanie's last.</span>

<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/777261-i-m-reading-it-now-it-s-ok-better-than">I&#39;m reading it now. It&#39;s ok, better than the first one. But, there are so many holes in the story. At what point does it become funny?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_777261'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F6427.Two_for_the_Dough">like</a></span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/68405506-mary"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1513300958i/68405506._UX100_CR0,9,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/68405506-mary">Mary</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    It's not meant to be a comedy per se, so it's best to put that expectation aside. I chuckled a couple times. I considered it a light-hearted romp and <a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    It's not meant to be a comedy per se, so it's best to put that expectation aside. I chuckled a couple times. I considered it a light-hearted romp and didn't look too deeply for flaws. My impression is that the writing is somewhere between a cozy mystery and detective fiction. I read this type of book when I need a quick, easy read in between meatier reads. The thing that bugged me the most was the whole damsel-in-distress thing. She keeps doing stupid, impulsive things and needs Morelli to continually save her. I've only read two of these. I hope she eventually gets her shit together.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>

  <span id="freeText7558343888428241682" style="display:none">I love this book!<br /> <br />One for the Money, as great as this series is, really didn’t show you the potential of laughter to come.<br /> <br />Two for the Dough changes everything! The relationship between Stephanie and Morelli will leave you smiling. All of the wonderful little things in a relationship that bugs you, you’ll find in theirs. The awkward moments to the pitter patter wonder moments.<br /> <br />Grandma Mazur really steps on stage with her need to pay her respects to the dead. Skipping her feet to help her granddaughter pursue the deadly criminals threatening her life, she finds herself injured and pissed. Playing Dirty Harry and being as sharp as a pistol, Mazur will bring a smile to your face.<br /> <br />Stephanie, still new at being a Bounty Hunter, second guesses her abilities. Lula will appear in this book and let the games begin! This book is just the start of a wonderfully HILARIOUS team!<br /> <br />I definitely recommend this book to anyone needing a smile. Mild violence. No sexual content.<br /> <br />Thumbs up to Janet Evanovich!<br /></span>

Sure there is the Scooby doo type mystery afoot in them but I find I’m more drawn to the personal interactions of the characters and the kooky stuff that happens along the way such as:<br/><br/>--- How much trouble a grandma cause at not just one but multiple viewings. <i>Granny Mazur rocks</i> <br/><br/>--- Chase scene through the mall in purple heels.<br/><br/>--- A big Buick that seems to have a mind of it’s own and can’t be stopped until it has crashed into at least one other car. <i>Her insur</i></span>

Sure there is the Scooby doo type mystery afoot in them but I find I’m more drawn to the personal interactions of the characters and the kooky stuff that happens along the way such as:<br /><br />--- How much trouble a grandma cause at not just one but multiple viewings. <i>Granny Mazur rocks</i> <br /><br />--- Chase scene through the mall in purple heels.<br /><br />--- A big Buick that seems to have a mind of it’s own and can’t be stopped until it has crashed into at least one other car. <i>Her insurance is going to be outrageous after this.</i><br /><br />--- Various body parts showing up unexpectedly. <i>one of them was definitely not Jewish</i><br /><br />--- An almost hot and heavy scene that turned pretty funny. <br /><br />Stephanie is a fledgling bounty hunter still learning the ropes. But she seems to stumble into all the right or wrong places as the case may be. This leads to hilarity and a little chaos but never really a dull moment. <br /><br />This is a bit dated since there are still answering machines, beepers, phone books and car phones but don’t let that discourage you it will remind you of a time where it was harder to get a hold of people and you couldn’t ask google everything.<br /><br />The mystery was okay and I did like how it ended but for me it is all about the characters, the semi-sexual tension happening and Stephanie doing silly things that sometimes go well but more often than not go horrible and hilariously wrong instead.<br /></span>

This one is all about her libido with </span>
  <span id="freeText7553925204140355453" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>
    <u>Review</u>
  </i>
</b><br />3 stars to book #2 in the Stephanie Plum mystery series, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6427.Two_for_the_Dough__Stephanie_Plum___2_" title="Two for the Dough (Stephanie Plum, #2) by Janet Evanovich" rel="nofollow noopener">Two for the Dough</a>, by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2384.Janet_Evanovich" title="Janet Evanovich" rel="nofollow noopener">Janet Evanovich</a>. Since I'm going back to complete reviews on all the books I've read, and there are over 20 in this series, it would be too boring to do a normal review... so I'll keep it short. A few fun things about this one:<br /><br />1. We're still getting to know how crazy Stephanie Plum is compared to everyone else. She's neurotic in a fun way -- sort of like I am.<br /><br />2. This one is all about her libido with Joe Morelli. What's more important... getting lucky or catching the criminal? She can't decide but Evanovich presents many funny romantic situations in this edition.<br /><br />3. Stephanie's cousin is hilarious. He's a creep. And I would not want to meet him in reality. But he provides necessary humor.<br /><br />4. Not knowing how to properly catch a criminal can really get her in hot water. The situations she finds herself in are just laugh out loud. I don't know how the writer keeps on coming up with them.<br /><br />5. We're learning a bit more about the dangers of Ranger. And I like it! He's someone you just never know what to expect... it could be good or it could be the good kind of bad.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1629066296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10199524436180844990">Not quite as good as the first one, but definitely fun!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"Sweetie, you are the worst bounty hunter in the history of the world."</i>
</b><br/><br/>This is true. Stephanie has settled into her life as a bounty hunter, but that doesn't mean she is necessarily good at it. She blunders her way through things, annoying the hell out of enough people to make sure she is targeted (not exactly on purpose. It just happens), and eventually things work out for her. Eventually. <br/><br/>In this book, she is looking for a cousin of Mo</span>
  <span id="freeText10199524436180844990" style="display:none">Not quite as good as the first one, but definitely fun!<br><br><b>
  <i>"Sweetie, you are the worst bounty hunter in the history of the world."</i>
</b><br><br>This is true. Stephanie has settled into her life as a bounty hunter, but that doesn't mean she is necessarily good at it. She blunders her way through things, annoying the hell out of enough people to make sure she is targeted (not exactly on purpose. It just happens), and eventually things work out for her. Eventually. <br><br>In this book, she is looking for a cousin of Morelli. This guy was supposed to be an easy pick-up, but things go downhill very quickly for Stephanie. <br><br><b>
  <i>"You're not doing too good here, babe," Morelli said. "You've had your car stolen, your apartment vandalized, and someone tried to snuff your hamster. Maybe you should drop back and punt."</i>
</b><br><br>No!! Not Rex! Poor little Rex never hurt anyone!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462428012i/18995438.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Shhhh, Rex! I'm trying to make you look good here!<br><br>And, unfortunately for Morelli, when things go downhill for Stephanie, his car seems to take the brunt of the bad juju. After getting his last car blown-up, she does a more methodical approach to ruining his present car in this book. Let's just say that her insurance must be sky-high. But, it's funny. Really funny.<br><br>Along with our mystery, and some slow-burn romance budding, we get treated to a lot of Grandma Mazur in this book. She is crazy in the best possible way. She has a way of causing mayhem at funeral parlors to such a degree that she has been dubbed "Granny Disaster". But, she just loves going to viewings, even if it's just to take a peek inside a closed casket.<br><br>The characters in this series are so great. I have never been anywhere near New Jersey, and my family is nothing like this, but it feels so real that I kind of wish I had. Everyone knows everyone and most of them are related in that big Italian family way. Stephanie's mother is constantly comparing her to other daughters and trying to set her up, along with worrying about what the neighbors will think.... Hmmm, never mind. I'm okay with being from a small family that minded their own business. But, it's hella funny to read about other people's dysfunctional relationships. <br><br>I need to keep reading this series because I am dying for Stephanie and Morelli to get together. He is circling her, but taking it very slowly. Come on already!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1462428012i/18995439.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

I asked him to help me because I was still learning the trade and needed all the help I could get. <b>His participation was in the ballpark of a pity fuck." </b> </i><br/><br/>Stephani is blessed with marvelous relatives and they all reside in a hopping neighborhood: <i>Grandma Mazur reads the ob</i></span>
  <span id="freeText3144230803332769179" style="display:none"><b> *** 4 *** </b><br /><br />A buddy read with the <b> BBB buddies </b> in December 2015<br /><br />Stephani is a bounty hunter in training. In her own words: <i> Ranger and I had a sort of loose partnership. Ranger was a genuine, cool-ass, numero-uno bounty hunter. I asked him to help me because I was still learning the trade and needed all the help I could get. <b>His participation was in the ballpark of a pity fuck." </b> </i><br /><br />Stephani is blessed with marvelous relatives and they all reside in a hopping neighborhood: <i>Grandma Mazur reads the obituary columns like they're part of the paper's entertainment section. Other communities have country clubs and fraternal orders. The burg has funeral parlors. <b>If people stopped dying the social life of the burg would come to a grinding halt."</b> </i> and <i> The traffic light turned green, and we all took off with our foot to the floor. I cut over two lanes to line up for the turnoff, beating out a Beemer. The driver flipped me the bird and blew his horn. I responded with some derisive Italian hand gestures and commented on his mother. Being born in Trenton carries a certain responsibility in these situations.</i><br /> Stephanie's' men are <b>Ranger: </b> <i> As far as I knew, Ranger wore only two colors: army green and bad-ass black. As always, he wore a jacket. This time the jacket was black leather. One could only guess what was hidden under the jacket. Probably enough firepower to wipe out a small European country. </i><br /><br />and <b>Morelli </b>, with whom she has some history...: <i>"You're lacking some critical attributes of a good bounty hunter," Morelli said.<br />"Like what?"<br />"Patience. Look at you. You're all tied up in knots."<br />He applied pressure at the base of my neck with his thumb and inched his way up to my hairline. My eyes drooped closed, and my breathing slowed.<br />"Feel good?" Morelli asked.<br />"Mmmmm."<br />He worked my shoulders with both hands. "You need to relax.""If I relax any more I'll melt and slide off the seat."<br />His hands stilled. "I like the melting part."<br />I turned my face toward him, and our eyes held.<br />"No," I said.<br />"Why not?"<br /><b>"Because I've already seen the movie, and I hate the ending."<br />"Maybe it'll have a different ending this time."<br />"Maybe it won't."</b><br />His thumb traced over the pulse in my neck, and when he spoke his voice was low and cat's-tongue rough. "How about the middle of the movie? Did you like the middle?"<br />The middle of the movie had smoked. "I've seen better middles." Morelli's face creased into a wide grin. "Liar." </i><br /><br />My, my, my.... Ooo, and there are bad guys, funerals and funeral homes, guns, perverted cousins and explosions as well... And Morelli... And Ranger... <br /><br /><br />Janet Evanovich is a master of the light and engaging mystery full of laughter, emotion, and characters which pop off the page and drive the story straight into our hearts. Nothing too complicated for a plot, nothing too tragic, and the tough moments are perfectly balanced with moments of tenderness and humor. When I read her books I can almost picture the people in them, since I have their counterparts among my family and friends. Once again, if a serious and deep suspense is your thing, this is not for you. However, if you like to read for the pleasure of relaxing with a book that brings a smile on your face and does not leave stains of darkness in your soul, this is what you need in your life - a Stephani Plum Book:):):)<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3144230803332769179" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12731536990611726812">Find all of my reviews at: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/'>http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br/><br/>Saturday I had to take the oldest boychild on a three-hour trek to play some ball in Middle of Nowhere, America. </a><br/><br/>I’m already well aware. This is my second go ‘round with Stephanie Plum, only this time I’m doing it via audio. It is true that Janet E. eventually began to follow a formula for later books in this series, but</span>
  <span id="freeText12731536990611726812" style="display:none">Find all of my reviews at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/">http://52bookminimum.blogspot.com/</a><br><br>Saturday I had to take the oldest boychild on a three-hour trek to play some ball in Middle of Nowhere, America. </a><br><br>I’m already well aware. This is my second go ‘round with Stephanie Plum, only this time I’m doing it via audio. It is true that Janet E. eventually began to follow a formula for later books in this series, but at #2 she hadn’t jumped the shark just yet. <i>Two for the Dough</i> has Stephanie tackling a case of missing economy caskets for Stiva’s funeral home as well as some “cop killer” bullets. An absentee Lula might lead superfans to scream . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538402795ra/26383206.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But remember, this one is from way back in the day when Evanovich probably thought there would be an eventual end to the series and was trying to write these things in real time so Lula would still be recovering from book #1. Also note if Evanovich hadn’t changed this approach we’d be reading about a 50-year old Stephanie still debating about having a baby with Ranger or Morelli or chatting it up with a decomposed Rex the 30-year old hamster. While this was missing Lula, it had plenty of Grandma Mazur to make up for things . . . . <br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538402795ra/26383207.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I’m handing out 4 Stars. <i>Two for the Dough</i> didn’t disappoint the second time, it’s fun to remember when these actually attempted at a plot and Lori Petty’s narration was again perfection. <br></span>

I have listen to this whole series on audiobooks, and the narrator of the audiobooks does a great job on this book. All the books in this series will make you laugh so much, and I will say the way to read these books is by audiobooks. All the characters are so fun and developed. I love this series so much. Stephanie Plum always gets into big messes, and she will make you laugh so much.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13696537558185147777">Well I didn't really like the first book, but I decided to give this series one more chance. I really wanted to like it. The series is so popular and loved by almost all cozy readers, so maybe it's just me.<br/><br/><br/>I don't know. I like the characters. They are fun. I love the idea of the series as well, but for some reason I can't get into the stories. The first book was slightly better than this one in my opinion.<br/><br/><br/>I probably won't continue this series, but there really isn't anything bad I can say about </span>
  <span id="freeText13696537558185147777" style="display:none">Well I didn't really like the first book, but I decided to give this series one more chance. I really wanted to like it. The series is so popular and loved by almost all cozy readers, so maybe it's just me.<br /><br /><br />I don't know. I like the characters. They are fun. I love the idea of the series as well, but for some reason I can't get into the stories. The first book was slightly better than this one in my opinion.<br /><br /><br />I probably won't continue this series, but there really isn't anything bad I can say about the books. I'm just not able to get into them.</span>

<div id="review_38941466" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/38941466" />
    <a title="Patrick Gibson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1758594-patrick-gibson"><img alt="Patrick Gibson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1228068580p2/1758594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/38941466?book_show_action=true">Nov 30, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick Gibson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick Gibson" href="/user/show/1758594-patrick-gibson">Patrick Gibson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1758594-patrick-gibson?shelf=estrogen">estrogen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer38941466" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11165839007817235768">It’s a world I am unfamiliar with—the world of Chic Lit (or, if you are over 18, I refer to as Clit Lit). Even though Janet Evanovich’s books take up at least three shelves at the local Barnes & Noble, I have never noticed. Probably because they are in the Mystery section which I pass through on my way to the Science Fiction wall. I don’t look to either side for fear of turning into a pillar of salt. But—(there is always a but) I am in a strange land under strange circumstances these days and St</span>
  <span id="freeText11165839007817235768" style="display:none">It’s a world I am unfamiliar with—the world of Chic Lit (or, if you are over 18, I refer to as Clit Lit). Even though Janet Evanovich’s books take up at least three shelves at the local Barnes &amp; Noble, I have never noticed. Probably because they are in the Mystery section which I pass through on my way to the Science Fiction wall. I don’t look to either side for fear of turning into a pillar of salt. But—(there is always a but) I am in a strange land under strange circumstances these days and Stephanie Plum has entered my life. It’s a good thing. At the moment I am taking care of my mom who is battling Parkinson’s, dementia and a bunch of other good stuff. When I first came into her house (after an absence of something like 20 years) I saw piles of books all over the place. I knew everything would be alright. Until I checked out the titles. They were all—and I mean all—mysteries. I never read murder mysteries unless written by Carl Hiaasen.<br />The inevitable day came when I found myself without a new book to read. With so many Evanovich books laying around I though what the hell—how bad can they be? Well campers, as millions of readers will attest: they are clever, fun and addictive. You don’t read the Stephanie Plum series for the plot necessarily, although some are clever. It’s the daffy characters and ‘I Love Lucy’ situations.<br />I am going to read them all (he says) and will add them to my bookshelf here only for my Boy Scout merit badge. No reviews. After you have read the first one, you know what you are going to get with the rest. So far, I am enjoying the hell out of them. I gotta say Janet—you can pen some hot eroticism when you want. The Stephanie Plum series is an industry unto itself, but don’t let this put you off from giving them a go. Oh yah, and start at the beginning. It’s important.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11165839007817235768" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=read-more-than-once">read-more-than-once</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=mystery-read-and-solved">mystery-read-and-solved</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=a-own-book-form">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=3-star">3-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3048260-erin-proud-book-hoarder?shelf=small-town">small-town</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer81509276" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11887916827265841140"><br/>This is one of those times where I remembered liking a book more the first time I read it. Re-reading it, I found I'm just not a big Evanovich fan. She has a style of cutesy, short and abbreviated writing style that doesn't suit me. I will say at least it's easy to read and quick to breeze through. <br/><br/>There IS genuine humor that works - I laughed out loud a few times - but some of it comes off as forced and a little contrived. Stephanie is motivated by the greed of success, but I don't see much els</span>
  <span id="freeText11887916827265841140" style="display:none"><br />This is one of those times where I remembered liking a book more the first time I read it. Re-reading it, I found I'm just not a big Evanovich fan. She has a style of cutesy, short and abbreviated writing style that doesn't suit me. I will say at least it's easy to read and quick to breeze through. <br /><br />There IS genuine humor that works - I laughed out loud a few times - but some of it comes off as forced and a little contrived. Stephanie is motivated by the greed of success, but I don't see much else about her as a realistic character. Morelli is probably the best part, as he's amusing too but his dialogue is well constructed (the scene with Ranger and the truck was probably the best part of the book.) I know many love the Grandmother, and she is cute, but she's also stereotypical - as is the mother and father.<br /><br />These books are fun - the plots are creative enough for this type, the humor is real, the writing easy to digest, characters enjoyable to a point....but it doesn't have a deep core or that much substance other than some predictable staples.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11887916827265841140" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1507335071?book_show_action=true">Jan 12, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gavin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gavin" href="/user/show/8192509-gavin">Gavin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1507335071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4498930418265963783">This was just as fun and entertaining as the first book in the <i>Stephanie Plum</i> series. <br/><br/>Rookie bounty hunter Stephanie Plum has her second major bail jumper in sight. Kenny Mancuso, cousin of Joe Morelli, is on the run after shooting his best friend. It seems a straight forward case to begin with, but Stephanie never expected cousin Kenny to be so crazy or to have to deal with the stuff he is caught up in. Lucky for her she has Joe, Ranger, and even Grandma Mazur to help her out! <br/><br/>I loved the story</span>
  <span id="freeText4498930418265963783" style="display:none">This was just as fun and entertaining as the first book in the <i>Stephanie Plum</i> series. <br /><br />Rookie bounty hunter Stephanie Plum has her second major bail jumper in sight. Kenny Mancuso, cousin of Joe Morelli, is on the run after shooting his best friend. It seems a straight forward case to begin with, but Stephanie never expected cousin Kenny to be so crazy or to have to deal with the stuff he is caught up in. Lucky for her she has Joe, Ranger, and even Grandma Mazur to help her out! <br /><br />I loved the story. It had a little bit of everything with action, humor, mystery, and even a hint of romance. The scenes between Joe and Stephanie are awesome. They have great chemistry and both are a touch on the crazy side so their interactions are frequently hilarious. <br /><br />Kenny was a crazed villain and it was engaging to follow Stephanie as she tried to bring him to justice while also trying to track down some missing coffins as a side job! <br /><br />Grandma Mazur was even more hilarious in this book than she was in the first. Stephanie definitely needs to bring her on more bounty hunts in the future.<br /><br />Rating: 3.5 stars.<br /><br />Audio Note: I'm getting more used to C. J. Critt and think she did a good job with this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4498930418265963783" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780684196381" href="/book/show/630833.Two_for_the_Dough">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Stephanie Plum fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tatiana by: </span>
      Heather
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=mysteries-thrillers-horror">mysteries-thrillers-horror</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer86485202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12267651703136764703">I think there is no need to rehash the synopsis of "Two for the Dough." All you need to know is that it is about military ammo, caskets, and severed body parts, all delivered with a unique burg flare. Otherwise the mystery (if it can even be called that) was unremarkable and never ended with a big revelation like you always expect mysteries to end. Basically, there was no real climax.<br/><br/>I liked this book slightly less than "One for the Money" and if I could, I'd rather give it 3.5 stars instead of </span>
  <span id="freeText12267651703136764703" style="display:none">I think there is no need to rehash the synopsis of "Two for the Dough." All you need to know is that it is about military ammo, caskets, and severed body parts, all delivered with a unique burg flare. Otherwise the mystery (if it can even be called that) was unremarkable and never ended with a big revelation like you always expect mysteries to end. Basically, there was no real climax.<br /><br />I liked this book slightly less than "One for the Money" and if I could, I'd rather give it 3.5 stars instead of 4. Everything about it - Grandma Mazur's antics, Morelli's smoldering hotness, Stephanie's happy-go-lucky attitude - were simply no longer fresh. The story was still entertaining and engaging in every possible way, but I just didn't find it as funny as its predecessor. It took Evanovich more than 150 pages to squeeze some chuckles out of me and I was seriously wary of Grandma's lines by the end of the book. <br /><br />However, I still enjoyed "Two for the Dough" quite a bit and will continue on with the series, but it is obvious to me that I can only take both Stephanie and the burg in small doses, with long breaks between the books. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12267651703136764703" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText11833488871134695898" style="display:none">I finished the second book of the Stephanie Plum series in about 3 days. I was very happy to see he is a part of the cast of characters that is going to be sticking around. He is a great character, mysterious, sexy character &amp; wow! I have never had a "crush" on a character in a book before but now I do!<br /><br />Plus the relationship/sexual tension that is going on between Stephanie &amp; Joe has me turning the pages as well. I keep wondering when they are going to do the deed, lol! Makes me wish I were Stephanie &amp; it also makes me wish Joe Morelli were real, lol!<br /><br />Aside from all that, Evanovich created another great plot &amp; the book never got boring. <br /><br />So far I'm enjoying the Stephanie Plum series!</span>

<div id="review_1417858768" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1417858768" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388694025p2/3344685.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1417858768?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/3344685-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-in-2015">read-in-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-kindle">books-i-own-kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3344685-sarah?shelf=books-i-own-print">books-i-own-print</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1417858768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10302305984540736614">Stephanie's latest skip should be easy to collar, local boy Kenny shot his best friend in the knee during an argument but it was only a minor incident and Moogey didn't even want to press charges so there is no need for him to do a disappearing act. Then, after Kenny misses his court date, Moogey is murdered and prime suspect Kenny falls completely off the radar. Not one to walk away from a case Stephanie becomes determined to track Kenny down but when her investigations lead her to a funeral pa</span>
  <span id="freeText10302305984540736614" style="display:none">Stephanie's latest skip should be easy to collar, local boy Kenny shot his best friend in the knee during an argument but it was only a minor incident and Moogey didn't even want to press charges so there is no need for him to do a disappearing act. Then, after Kenny misses his court date, Moogey is murdered and prime suspect Kenny falls completely off the radar. Not one to walk away from a case Stephanie becomes determined to track Kenny down but when her investigations lead her to a funeral parlour with a missing batch of caskets and then various body parts start going missing things get much more complicated.<br /><br />This series is just so much fun to read, it's pure entertainment from first page to last and every book has me giggling the whole way through. I must be on my third read through of the early books in the series yet I never get tired of them. Stephanie is such a likeable character, she has a knack for finding trouble and she gets herself into the most ridiculous and crazy situations but I love her all the more because of it. The best thing about these books are the characters, Stephanie's whole family is brilliant but it's Grandma Mazur who steals the show in this book, she manages to cause even more trouble than Stephanie and that's really saying something. I love the things she comes out with and I could happily quote half the book in this review.<br /><br />I also love the men in the series, Ranger is still pretty much a complete mystery at this point but I know from later books how brilliant he is and I'm looking forward to unravelling him a bit more. Morelli is fantastic and the chemistry between him and Stephanie is great, they have a very complicated history so she is very wary of trusting him but it's obvious he's more than a little interested and I'm enjoying watching their relationship develop.<br /><br />I've been wanting to reread these books and catch up with the most recent releases (I think I got to about book 15 in my last read through) for a long time now so I'm glad to be reading the series with a group of friends. At one book a month this is going to be a very long ongoing project but I'm actually enjoying having at least one really funny and light hearted read to look forward to each month and I think having such a relaxed schedule is going to make it much easier to stick to. Roll on January so I can get started on <b>Three to Get Deadly</b>!<br />_______________________________________<br /><br />Series group read with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies, Books &amp; Baubles</a> starts 1st December. We're planning on reading one book a month so it'll be easy to keep up with if anyone else wants to join us :o)</span>
  <a data-text-id="10302305984540736614" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

People will think you’re mad because you laugh to death by yourself.<br /><br />This time Stephanie and the Buick did it for me. What’s with that car? And poor Morelli, when he’s near Stephanie his police car is always in danger. Just like his previous car.<br />Grandma Mazur was also a lot of fun. I think she’s the craziest character of the series and that’s something since everyone in Trenton has serious issues 😂<br /><br />I am also so so so in love with the relationship between Stephanie and Morelli. Morelli is &lt;3&lt;3&lt;3<br /><br /><i>”You left me standing bare-assed in the middle of the street!”<br />“I gave you your gun, didn’t I?”<br />Morelli grinned. “You’re going to give me more than that, cupcake.”<br />“Forget it.”<br />“Not likely,” Morelli said. “You owe me.” [...]<br />I pushed him out of my foyer, into the hall, slammed the door closed, and threw the bolt. I pressed my nose to the door and looked through the peephole.<br />Morelli grinned at me.<br />“This is war,” I yelled through the door.<br />“Luck for me,” Morelli said. “I give good war.”</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9852971953809505368" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1456854049506985244">Now Stephanie's back, armed with attitude -- not to mention stun guns, defense sprays, killer flashlights, and her trusty .38, Stephanie is after a new bail jumper, Kenny Mancuso, a boy from Trenton's burg. He's fresh out of the army, suspiciously wealthy, and he's just shot his best friend.<br/><br/>With her bounty hunter pal Ranger stepping in occasionally to advise her, Stephanie staggers kneedeep in corpses and caskets as she traipses through back streets, dark alleys, and funeral parlors.<br/><br/>And nobody k</span>
  <span id="freeText1456854049506985244" style="display:none">Now Stephanie's back, armed with attitude -- not to mention stun guns, defense sprays, killer flashlights, and her trusty .38, Stephanie is after a new bail jumper, Kenny Mancuso, a boy from Trenton's burg. He's fresh out of the army, suspiciously wealthy, and he's just shot his best friend.<br /><br />With her bounty hunter pal Ranger stepping in occasionally to advise her, Stephanie staggers kneedeep in corpses and caskets as she traipses through back streets, dark alleys, and funeral parlors.<br /><br />And nobody knows funeral parlors better than Stephanie's irrepressible Grandma Mazur, a lady whose favorite pastime is grabbing a front-row seat at a neighborhood wake. So Stephanie uses Grandma as a cover to follow leads, but loses control when Grandma warms to the action, packing a cool pistol. Much to the family's chagrin, Stephanie and Granny may soon have the elusive Kenny in their sights.<br /><br />Fast-talking, slow-handed vice cop Joe Morelli joins in the case, since the prey happens to be his young cousin. And if the assignment calls for an automobile stakeout for two with the woman who puts his libido in overdrive, Morelli's not one to object.<br /><br />Low on expertise but learning fast, high on resilience, and despite the help she gets from friends and relatives, Stephanie eventually must face the danger alone when embalmed body parts begin to arrive on her doorstep and she's targeted for a nasty death by the most loathsome adversary she's ever encountered. Another case like this and she'll be a real pro.<br /><br />Two for the Dough is irresistible fun and powerful suspense entertainment from an acclaimed author who is already a national star.<br /><br />This book was as wonderful, fun, action-packed, suspenseful, and enjoyable as the very first in the series. Stephanie and all the other characters have so much voice and they're hilarious. This series is amazing and I'm so glad I've chosen to read it.</span>

<div id="review_467391049" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/467391049" />
    <a title="Steph" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4215697-steph"><img alt="Steph" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1346102450p2/4215697.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/467391049?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph" href="/user/show/4215697-steph">Steph</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer467391049" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7082759692467579667"> I really enjoyed this book.<br/><br/> Kenny Mancuso has shot his old friend (Moogey) and has skipped bail, so Steph is out on the case to bring him in. Simple, right? <b>Wrong!</b><br/> Turns out Kenny is frickin bat-shit crazy. <br/>He hurts, threatens and beats anyone who get's in his way (including old ladies, but more on that later), he cut his own damn finger off to see what would happen...<br/> Honestly, he's a fruitcake!<br/> <br/> The other <i>'bad guy'</i> in this book is Spiro, who works in his dad's funeral home. Things go from bad</span>
  <span id="freeText7082759692467579667" style="display:none"> I really enjoyed this book.<br /><br /> Kenny Mancuso has shot his old friend (Moogey) and has skipped bail, so Steph is out on the case to bring him in. Simple, right? <b>Wrong!</b><br /> Turns out Kenny is frickin bat-shit crazy. <br />He hurts, threatens and beats anyone who get's in his way (including old ladies, but more on that later), he cut his own damn finger off to see what would happen...<br /> Honestly, he's a fruitcake!<br /> <br /> The other <i>'bad guy'</i> in this book is Spiro, who works in his dad's funeral home. Things go from bad to worse, quickly. When 24 coffins go missing... <br /> Kenny thinks that Spiro has taken something that belongs to him and goes crazy. He starts cutting body parts off the dead people and sending them in the mail, like some poor dead guys penis! *shudders*<br /> <br />The story about Kenny, Spiro and Moogey was great. A little simple, but nothing wrong with that.<br /><br /> One thing about this book that had me really divided? <i>Steph and Morelli.</i><br /> I was reading so fast, always trying to get to their scenes together. I love them so much and am desperate to see them get closer, for them to take the next step. I don't think that's the Authors problem, I think that's just me being a smutty cow. LOL. I was repeatedly disappointed with the <i>lack of 'sexy-time'</i>, however, when they are together I cannot stop smiling and I laugh non-stop. That makes up for it, almost.<br /><br /> 'He took a step closer and sniffed. <i>"I smell chocolate."<br /> "I had half a KitKat."<br /> "I don't suppose you have the other half?"<br /> "I ate it earlier."<br /> "Too bad. I might have been able to remember some crucial piece of information if I had a KitKat."</i><br /> So stupid. LOL<br /><br /> I loved the way that Morelli just kept showing up at her parent's house for dinner. Everyine says he's a 'ladies’ man', that he sleeps around. But all I've seen is Morelli taking care of her, making sure she's safe. Taking her home and staying for pizza and beer and later going home. He has been around her for months now and there have been no signs at all that, he has been anywhere near another woman. <br /> I adore him, the way he flirts with Steph and kisses her when she least expects it. He's unpredictable and spontaneous.<br /> I am dying for them to be together :)<br /><br /> Steph's mother is really great.<br /> <i>"What's this outfit?"</i> my mother demanded. <i>"Can't you afford clothes? Are you wearing other people's? Frank, give Stephanie some money. She needs to buy clothes."</i><br /> Love her.<br /> <br /><br /> <b>Grandma Mazur was amazing.</b>She's so annoying, but hilarious at the same time. Most of the times I was laughing were because of something ridiculous she has done. Especially in the funeral home, where she loved to go for regular viewings, whether she knew the deceased or not. LOL<br /><br /> 'Grandma straightened and turned to face us. <i>"Well, will you look at this,"</i> she said, holding an object the size of a Tootsie Roll in her hand. <i>"His finger came off."</i><br /> Mrs. Mackey fainted crash onto the floor, and Marjorie Boyer ran screaming out of the room.'<br /> Ahahaha.<br /><br /> I just have to finish this review with my favourite part of the entire book. I was wetting myself with laughter. <br /> Morelli was turning a blind-eye while Steph did things her <i>'not so legal'</i> way, and had an accident.<br /> <br /> 'Morelli shined a flashlight in my eyes. <i>"You sure you're okay?"<br /> "What kind of dog do you think it was?"<br /> "A big dog."<br /> "What kind?"<br /> "Rottweiler. Male. Old and overweight. Bad teeth. Ate a lot of tuna fish."</i><br /> I started to cry.<br /> <i>"Oh Jeez,"</i> Morelli said. <i>"Don't cry. I hate when you cry."<br /> "I've got rottweiler shit in my hair."</i><br /> He used his thumb to wipe the tears from my cheeks. <i>"It's okay, honey. It's really not so bad. I was kidding about the tuna."</i><br /> <br /> Her flapping around with shit in her hair in that alley was so damn funny :)<br /><br /> I will definitely continue on with this series.<br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="7082759692467579667" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16645482181508302067">This is one of my favorite series! Stephanie Plum is hilarious, and her quirky interactions with her family, coworkers and friends often have me laughing out loud. She's a determined rascal, and as a relatively new bounty hunter, she manages to round-up the bad guys, although in very unconventional and inventive ways. In this story, she has a surprising ally and the situations they encounter are wildly entertaining. I simply could not stop reading ^..^</span>

<div id="review_85562818" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/85562818" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2098381-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474068564p2/2098381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/85562818?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780312948962" href="/book/show/40342.Two_for_the_Dough">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer85562818" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12751138581275282830">I enjoyed <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money__A_Stephanie_Plum_Novel___1_' title='One for the Money (A Stephanie Plum Novel, #1) by Janet Evanovich' rel='nofollow noopener'>One for the Money</a>. The plot was entertaining, the setting was familiar in its otherness, and the characters were likable, well drawn and relatable. Furthermore, Stephanie Plum, the heroine, was rather humorous when remarking on the going’s on of the Berg and her family, and made me giggle at the situations she managed to find herself in. The pace was perfect for turning pages quickly, and before I knew it, I had completed the book. Naturally I wanted to keep reading, though I admit, I </span>
  <span id="freeText12751138581275282830" style="display:none">I enjoyed <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money__A_Stephanie_Plum_Novel___1_" title="One for the Money (A Stephanie Plum Novel, #1) by Janet Evanovich" rel="nofollow noopener">One for the Money</a>. The plot was entertaining, the setting was familiar in its otherness, and the characters were likable, well drawn and relatable. Furthermore, Stephanie Plum, the heroine, was rather humorous when remarking on the going’s on of the Berg and her family, and made me giggle at the situations she managed to find herself in. The pace was perfect for turning pages quickly, and before I knew it, I had completed the book. Naturally I wanted to keep reading, though I admit, I was just expecting more of the same. Surprisingly enough, Two for the Dough was significantly better.<br /><br />The first 30 or so pages were much like book one. Similar commentary, reintroduction to characters introduced to us in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6853.One_for_the_Money__A_Stephanie_Plum_Novel___1_" title="One for the Money (A Stephanie Plum Novel, #1) by Janet Evanovich" rel="nofollow noopener">One for the Money</a>, Stephanie fumbling around in her new role as bounty hunter, etc. I was a bit worried that my only comic relief would come from Grandma Mazur, not that that is a bad thing, she is just a bit outlandish. But by page 50 or so, Stephanie pulled through. I was pleased to see that she has maintained her bitter, party of one persona without seeming bitter. Not sure how that works, but she manages to pull it off. The tension between her and Morelli is mounting, climaxing in one laugh out loud scenario that had me near tears. Oh how I hope I someday have the opportunity to do that myself, or perhaps maybe not. Additionally, the “mystery” of this book is significantly more intriguing, making the book all that more enjoyable.<br /><br />I can’t believe I’m reading a book where male members are sent through the mail, endearing characters come in the form of overweight ex-ho’s, and funeral viewings are a form of social entertainment. Nonetheless, these books are laugh out loud funny, and I cannot wait to start <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6854.Three_To_Get_Deadly__A_Stephanie_Plum_Novel___3_" title="Three To Get Deadly (A Stephanie Plum Novel, #3) by Janet Evanovich" rel="nofollow noopener">Three to get Deadly</a>. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12751138581275282830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7549316270573307280">Rating: 4/5<br/><br/>Stephanie Plum is the new bounty hunter in Trenton, and after her first big case she is going after some more easy targets. Kenny Mancuso was supposed to be one of those easy targets but she can't seem to find him anywhere and Joe Morelli, her old fling, cop and Kenny's cousin seems to be following her. Stephanie will go from stake outs to funeral homes to find Kenny and figure out why he doesn't want to be found.<br/><br/>This was the first Stephanie Plum novel I read and I can't say it disapp</span>
  <span id="freeText7549316270573307280" style="display:none">Rating: 4/5<br /><br />Stephanie Plum is the new bounty hunter in Trenton, and after her first big case she is going after some more easy targets. Kenny Mancuso was supposed to be one of those easy targets but she can't seem to find him anywhere and Joe Morelli, her old fling, cop and Kenny's cousin seems to be following her. Stephanie will go from stake outs to funeral homes to find Kenny and figure out why he doesn't want to be found.<br /><br />This was the first Stephanie Plum novel I read and I can't say it disappointed me at all. I've watched the movie One For The Money over a dozen times and I always wanted to see more of Stephanie and her adventures. I was kind of skeptical picking up this one without reading the previous one but, even though there were a few changes, it wasn't hard to keep at all. <br /><br />Stephanie was as hilarious as I remembered and I enjoyed her every step of the way. The mystery behind Kenny was quite interesting. And the interactions with Joe were pure perfection. I love their dynamic. I am glad I found a series like this one and wait to read more of Stephanie's adventures.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('drKbuSq/Xv5Fu0Fz5cC6qTwwXJDg+vRAMtvtvUYkHGv9O+/LxsjPkv8AnZ8MYib5GGhhNsiIkrRPQ+mjeYz34Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('QsZ3HXnW5uo+2iI+cZ3gJ/yZbY+eAWOe09HabIgx75jJTwNvlaF3hoRh/tKYP3x32MFQKbZzBWquSd5yt5kEEg==')})
  }

In The Scam, Nicolas Fox and Kate O’Hare, a criminal put to work by the United States Federal Bureau of Investigation and the agent assigned to keep him in check as he deploys his talents for his country, investigate the international gambling operations of Evan Trace, whose full-service casinos serve as a means to launder the money made by criminal and terrorist groups. In a series of manipulations that see power dynamics shift wildly, Fox and O’Hare manage to turn Trace into an informant and, along the way, undermine a Hawaiian criminal enterprise.
